style="float:right;font-size:95%;">*<i><a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_glaciation" title="Timeline of glaciation">Ice Ages</a></i></div></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In contrast to <a href="/wiki/Evolutionary_history_of_plants" title="Evolutionary history of plants">plants</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evolutionary_history_of_life" title="Evolutionary history of life">animals</a>, the early fossil record of the fungi is meager. Factors that likely contribute to the under-representation of fungal species among fossils include the nature of fungal <a href="/wiki/Sporocarp_(fungi)" title="Sporocarp (fungi)">fruiting bodies</a>, which are soft, fleshy, and easily degradable tissues and the microscopic dimensions of most fungal structures, which therefore are not readily evident. Fungal fossils are difficult to distinguish from those of other microbes, and are most easily identified when they resemble <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extant_taxon" title="Extant taxon">extant</a> fungi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Donoghue2004_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Donoghue2004-115">[115]</a></sup> Often recovered from a <a href="/wiki/Permineralization" title="Permineralization">permineralized</a> plant or animal host, these samples are typically studied by making thin-section preparations that can be examined with <a href="/wiki/Optical_microscope" title="Optical microscope">light microscopy</a> or <a href="/wiki/Transmission_electron_microscopy" title="Transmission electron microscopy">transmission electron microscopy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Researchers study <a href="/wiki/Compression_fossil" title="Compression fossil">compression fossils</a> by dissolving the surrounding matrix with acid and then using light or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scanning_electron_microscopy" title="Scanning electron microscopy">scanning electron microscopy</a> to examine surface details.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prototaxites_milwaukeensis.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="7000" data-file-width="4120" decoding="async" height="374" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Prototaxites_milwaukeensis.jpg/220px-Prototaxites_milwaukeensis.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Prototaxites_milwaukeensis.jpg/330px-Prototaxites_milwaukeensis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Prototaxites_milwaukeensis.jpg/440px-Prototaxites_milwaukeensis.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Prototaxites_milwaukeensis.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Prototaxites" title="Prototaxites">Prototaxites</a> milwaukeensis</i> (Penhallow, 1908)—a Middle <a href="/wiki/Devonian" title="Devonian">Devonian</a> fungus from <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin" title="Wisconsin">Wisconsin</a></div></div></div>
<p>The earliest fossils possessing features typical of fungi date to the <a href="/wiki/Paleoproterozoic" title="Paleoproterozoic">Paleoproterozoic</a> era, some <span class="nourlexpansion plainlinks" style="white-space:nowrap;"><a class="external text" href="http://tools.wmflabs.org/timescale/?Ma=2,400">2,400</a> million years ago</span> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annum" title="Annum">Ma</a>); these multicellular <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benthic" title="Benthic">benthic</a> organisms had filamentous structures capable of <a href="/wiki/Anastomosis" title="Anastomosis">anastomosis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> Other studies (2009) estimate the arrival of fungal organisms at about 760–1060<span class="nowrap"> </span>Ma on the basis of comparisons of the rate of evolution in closely related groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lucking2009_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lucking2009-119">[119]</a></sup> For much of the <a href="/wiki/Paleozoic" title="Paleozoic">Paleozoic</a> Era (542–251<span class="nowrap"> </span>Ma), the fungi appear to have been aquatic and consisted of organisms similar to the extant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chytrid" title="Chytrid">chytrids</a> in having flagellum-bearing spores.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-James2006b_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-James2006b-120">[120]</a></sup> The evolutionary adaptation from an aquatic to a terrestrial lifestyle necessitated a diversification of ecological strategies for obtaining nutrients, including <a href="/wiki/Parasitism" title="Parasitism">parasitism</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saphrotrophic_nutrition" title="Saphrotrophic nutrition">saprobism</a>, and the development of <a href="/wiki/Mutualism_(biology)" title="Mutualism (biology)">mutualistic</a> relationships such as <a href="/wiki/Mycorrhiza" title="Mycorrhiza">mycorrhiza</a> and lichenization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Studies suggest that the ancestral ecological state of the <a href="/wiki/Ascomycota" title="Ascomycota">Ascomycota</a> was saprobism, and that independent <a href="/wiki/Lichen" title="Lichen">lichenization</a> events have occurred multiple times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schoch2009_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schoch2009-122">[122]</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2019, scientists reported the discovery of a <a href="/wiki/Fossil" title="Fossil">fossilized</a> fungus, named <i><a href="/wiki/Ourasphaira_giraldae" title="Ourasphaira giraldae">Ourasphaira giraldae</a></i>, in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Canada" title="Northern Canada">Canadian Arctic</a>, that may have grown on land a billion years ago, well before <a href="/wiki/Plant" title="Plant">plants</a> were living on land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20190522_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20190522-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAT-20190522_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-NAT-20190522-124">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ars_Technica_2019_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ars_Technica_2019-125">[125]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Permineralization#Pyritization" title="Permineralization">Pyritized</a> fungus-like <a href="/wiki/Microfossil" title="Microfossil">microfossils</a> preserved in the basal Ediacaran Doushantuo Formation (~635 Ma) have been reported in South China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Earlier, it had been presumed that the fungi colonized the land during the <a href="/wiki/Cambrian" title="Cambrian">Cambrian</a> (542–488.3<span class="nowrap"> </span>Ma), also long before land plants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brundrett2002_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brundrett2002-127">[127]</a></sup> Fossilized hyphae and spores recovered from the <a href="/wiki/Ordovician" title="Ordovician">Ordovician</a> of Wisconsin (460<span class="nowrap"> </span>Ma) resemble modern-day <a href="/wiki/Glomerales" title="Glomerales">Glomerales</a>, and existed at a time when the land flora likely consisted of only non-vascular <a href="/wiki/Bryophyte" title="Bryophyte">bryophyte</a>-like plants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Redecker2000_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-Redecker2000-128">[128]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Prototaxites" title="Prototaxites">Prototaxites</a>, which was probably a fungus or lichen, would have been the tallest organism of the late <a href="/wiki/Silurian" title="Silurian">Silurian</a> and early <a href="/wiki/Devonian" title="Devonian">Devonian</a>. Fungal fossils do not become common and uncontroversial until the early <a href="/wiki/Devonian" title="Devonian">Devonian</a> (416–359.2<span class="nowrap"> </span>Ma), when they occur abundantly in the <a href="/wiki/Rhynie_chert" title="Rhynie chert">Rhynie chert</a>, mostly as <a href="/wiki/Zygomycota" title="Zygomycota">Zygomycota</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chytridiomycota" title="Chytridiomycota">Chytridiomycota</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brundrett2002_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-Brundrett2002-127">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Taylor1996_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor1996-129">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dotzler2009_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dotzler2009-130">[130]</a></sup> At about this same time, approximately 400<span class="nowrap"> </span>Ma, the Ascomycota and Basidiomycota diverged,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Taylor2006_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor2006-131">[131]</a></sup> and all modern <a href="/wiki/Class_(biology)" title="Class (biology)">classes</a> of fungi were present by the Late <a href="/wiki/Carboniferous" title="Carboniferous">Carboniferous</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pennsylvanian_(geology)" title="Pennsylvanian (geology)">Pennsylvanian</a>, 318.1–299<span class="nowrap"> </span>Ma).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-urlFungi_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-urlFungi-132">[132]</a></sup>
</p><p>Lichens formed a component of the early terrestrial ecosystems, and the estimated age of the oldest terrestrial lichen fossil is 415<span class="nowrap"> </span>Ma;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Honegger_et_al._2013_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Honegger_et_al._2013-133">[133]</a></sup> this date roughly corresponds to the age of the oldest known <a href="/wiki/Sporocarp_(fungi)" title="Sporocarp (fungi)">sporocarp</a> fossil, a <i><a href="/wiki/Paleopyrenomycites" title="Paleopyrenomycites">Paleopyrenomycites</a></i> species found in the Rhynie Chert.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Taylor2005_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor2005-134">[134]</a></sup> The oldest fossil with microscopic features resembling modern-day basidiomycetes is <i>Palaeoancistrus</i>, found permineralized with a <a href="/wiki/Fern" title="Fern">fern</a> from the Pennsylvanian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dennis1970_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dennis1970-135">[135]</a></sup> Rare in the fossil record are the Homobasidiomycetes (a <a href="/wiki/Taxon" title="Taxon">taxon</a> roughly equivalent to the mushroom-producing species of the <a href="/wiki/Agaricomycetes" title="Agaricomycetes">Agaricomycetes</a>). Two <a href="/wiki/Amber" title="Amber">amber</a>-preserved specimens provide evidence that the earliest known mushroom-forming fungi (the extinct species <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archaeomarasmius_leggetti" title="Archaeomarasmius leggetti">Archaeomarasmius leggetti</a></i>) appeared during the late <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous" title="Cretaceous">Cretaceous</a>, 90<span class="nowrap"> </span>Ma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hibbett1995_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hibbett1995-136">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hibbett1997_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hibbett1997-137">[137]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some time after the <a href="/wiki/Permian%E2%80%93Triassic_extinction_event" title="Permian–Triassic extinction event">Permian–Triassic extinction event</a> (251.4<span class="nowrap"> </span>Ma), a fungal spike (originally thought to be an extraordinary abundance of fungal spores in <a href="/wiki/Sediment" title="Sediment">sediments</a>) formed, suggesting that fungi were the dominant life form at this time, representing nearly 100% of the available <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fossil_record" title="Fossil record">fossil record</a> for this period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eshet1995_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eshet1995-138">[138]</a></sup> However, the relative proportion of fungal spores relative to spores formed by <a href="/wiki/Algae" title="Algae">algal</a> species is difficult to assess,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foster2002_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-Foster2002-139">[139]</a></sup> the spike did not appear worldwide,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LopezGomez2005_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-LopezGomez2005-140">[140]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Looy2005_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-Looy2005-141">[141]</a></sup> and in many places it did not fall on the Permian–Triassic boundary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ward2005_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ward2005-142">[142]</a></sup>
</p><p>Sixty-five million years ago, immediately after the <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous%E2%80%93Paleogene_extinction_event" title="Cretaceous–Paleogene extinction event">Cretaceous–Paleogene extinction event</a> that famously killed off most dinosaurs, there was a dramatic increase in evidence of fungi; apparently the death of most plant and animal species led to a huge fungal bloom like "a massive compost heap".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxonomy">Taxonomy</span></h2>
<p>Although commonly included in botany curricula and textbooks, fungi are more closely related to <a href="/wiki/Animal" title="Animal">animals</a> than to plants and are placed with the animals in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monophyletic" title="Monophyletic">monophyletic</a> group of <a href="/wiki/Opisthokont" title="Opisthokont">opisthokonts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ShalchianTabrizi2008_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-ShalchianTabrizi2008-144">[144]</a></sup> Analyses using <a href="/wiki/Molecular_phylogenetics" title="Molecular phylogenetics">molecular phylogenetics</a> support a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monophyletic_group" title="Monophyletic group">monophyletic</a> origin of fungi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hibbett2007_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hibbett2007-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Li_et_al_2021_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-Li_et_al_2021-145">[145]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Taxonomy_(biology)" title="Taxonomy (biology)">taxonomy</a> of fungi is in a state of constant flux, especially due to research based on DNA comparisons. These current phylogenetic analyses often overturn classifications based on older and sometimes less discriminative methods based on morphological features and biological species concepts obtained from experimental <a href="/wiki/Mating" title="Mating">matings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is no unique generally accepted system at the higher taxonomic levels and there are frequent name changes at every level, from species upwards. Efforts among researchers are now underway to establish and encourage usage of a unified and more consistent <a href="/wiki/Botanical_nomenclature" title="Botanical nomenclature">nomenclature</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hibbett2007_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hibbett2007-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Celio2006_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-Celio2006-147">[147]</a></sup> Until relatively recent (2012) changes to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Code_of_Nomenclature_for_algae,_fungi_and_plants" title="International Code of Nomenclature for algae, fungi and plants">International Code of Nomenclature for algae, fungi and plants</a>, fungal species could also have multiple scientific names depending on their life cycle and mode (sexual or asexual) of reproduction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rossman_2014_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rossman_2014-148">[148]</a></sup> Web sites such as <a href="/wiki/Index_Fungorum" title="Index Fungorum">Index Fungorum</a> and <a href="/wiki/MycoBank" title="MycoBank">MycoBank</a> are officially recognized <a href="/wiki/Nomenclature_codes" title="Nomenclature codes">nomenclatural</a> repositories and list current names of fungal species (with cross-references to older <a href="/wiki/Synonym_(taxonomy)" title="Synonym (taxonomy)">synonyms</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Redhead_&amp;_Norvell_2013_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-Redhead_&amp;_Norvell_2013-149">[149]</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2007 classification of Kingdom Fungi is the result of a large-scale collaborative research effort involving dozens of mycologists and other scientists working on fungal taxonomy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hibbett2007_50-3"><a href="#cite_note-Hibbett2007-50">[50]</a></sup> It recognizes seven <a href="/wiki/Phylum" title="Phylum">phyla</a>, two of which—the Ascomycota and the Basidiomycota—are contained within a branch representing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subkingdom" title="Subkingdom">subkingdom</a> <a href="/wiki/Dikarya" title="Dikarya">Dikarya</a>, the most species rich and familiar group, including all the mushrooms, most food-spoilage molds, most plant pathogenic fungi, and the beer, wine, and bread yeasts. The accompanying <a href="/wiki/Cladogram" title="Cladogram">cladogram</a> depicts the major fungal <a href="/wiki/Taxon" title="Taxon">taxa</a> and their relationship to opisthokont and unikont organisms, based on the work of Philippe Silar,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Silar2016_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-Silar2016-150">[150]</a></sup> "The Mycota: A Comprehensive Treatise on Fungi as Experimental Systems for Basic and Applied Research"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MycotaVIIS&amp;E_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-MycotaVIIS&amp;E-151">[151]</a></sup> and Tedersoo et al. 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> The lengths of the branches are not proportional to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evolutionary" title="Evolutionary">evolutionary</a> distances.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r984819063">.mw-parser-output table.clade{border-spacing:0;margin:0;font-size:100%;line-height:100%;border-collapse:separate;width:auto}.mw-parser-output table.clade table.clade{width:100%;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-label{width:0.7em;padding:0 0.15em;vertical-align:bottom;text-align:center;border-left:1px solid;border-bottom:1px solid;white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-fixed-width{overflow:hidden;text-overflow:ellipsis}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-fixed-width:hover{overflow:visible}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-label.first{border-left:none;border-right:none}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-label.reverse{border-left:none;border-right:1px solid}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-slabel{padding:0 0.15em;vertical-align:top;text-align:center;border-left:1px solid;white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-slabel:hover{overflow:visible}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-slabel.last{border-left:none;border-right:none}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-slabel.reverse{border-left:none;border-right:1px solid}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-bar{vertical-align:middle;text-align:left;padding:0 0.5em;position:relative}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-bar.reverse{text-align:right;position:relative}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-leaf{border:0;padding:0;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-leafR{border:0;padding:0;text-align:right}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-leaf.reverse{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output table.clade:hover span.linkA{background-color:yellow}.mw-parser-output table.clade:hover span.linkB{background-color:green}</style>

<tbody><tr>
<td class="clade-label first">Chytridiomyceta
