//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Ganoderma_lucidum_01.jpg/280px-Ganoderma_lucidum_01.jpg 2x" width="140"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CordycepsSinensis.jpg"><img alt="Two dried yellow-orange caterpillars, one with a curly grayish fungus growing out of one of its ends. The grayish fungus is roughly equal to or slightly greater in length than the caterpillar, and tapers in thickness to a narrow end." data-file-height="1136" data-file-width="1948" decoding="async" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/CordycepsSinensis.jpg/180px-CordycepsSinensis.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/CordycepsSinensis.jpg/270px-CordycepsSinensis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/CordycepsSinensis.jpg/360px-CordycepsSinensis.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">The fungi <i><a href="/wiki/Ganoderma_lucidum" title="Ganoderma lucidum">Ganoderma lucidum</a></i> (left) and <i><a href="/wiki/Ophiocordyceps_sinensis" title="Ophiocordyceps sinensis">Ophiocordyceps sinensis</a></i> (right) are used in traditional medicine practices</div></div></div></div>
<p>Certain mushrooms are used as supposed therapeutics in <a href="/wiki/Traditional_medicine" title="Traditional medicine">folk medicine practices</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_medicine" title="Traditional Chinese medicine">traditional Chinese medicine</a>. Mushrooms with a history of such use include <i><a href="/wiki/Agaricus_subrufescens" title="Agaricus subrufescens">Agaricus subrufescens</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hetland2008_246-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hetland2008-246">[246]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Firenzuoli2008_250-0"><a href="#cite_note-Firenzuoli2008-250">[250]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Ganoderma_lucidum" title="Ganoderma lucidum">Ganoderma lucidum</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lu_et_al._2020_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lu_et_al._2020-251">[251]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Ophiocordyceps_sinensis" title="Ophiocordyceps sinensis">Ophiocordyceps sinensis</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Olatunji_et_al._2018_252-0"><a href="#cite_note-Olatunji_et_al._2018-252">[252]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultured_foods">Cultured foods</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Baker%27s_yeast" title="Baker's yeast">Baker's yeast</a> or <i><a href="/wiki/Saccharomyces_cerevisiae" title="Saccharomyces cerevisiae">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</a></i>, a unicellular fungus, is used to make <a href="/wiki/Bread" title="Bread">bread</a> and other wheat-based products, such as <a href="/wiki/Pizza" title="Pizza">pizza</a> dough and <a href="/wiki/Dumpling" title="Dumpling">dumplings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kulp2000_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kulp2000-253">[253]</a></sup> Yeast species of the genus <i><a href="/wiki/Saccharomyces" title="Saccharomyces">Saccharomyces</a></i> are also used to produce <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage" title="Alcoholic beverage">alcoholic beverages</a> through fermentation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Piskur2006_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-Piskur2006-254">[254]</a></sup> Shoyu koji mold (<i><a href="/wiki/Aspergillus_oryzae" title="Aspergillus oryzae">Aspergillus oryzae</a></i>) is an essential ingredient in brewing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shoyu" title="Shoyu">Shoyu</a> (<a href="/wiki/Soy_sauce" title="Soy sauce">soy sauce</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Sake" title="Sake">sake</a>, and the preparation of <a href="/wiki/Miso" title="Miso">miso</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abe2006_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-Abe2006-255">[255]</a></sup> while <i><a href="/wiki/Rhizopus" title="Rhizopus">Rhizopus</a></i> species are used for making <a href="/wiki/Tempeh" title="Tempeh">tempeh</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hachmeister1993_256-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hachmeister1993-256">[256]</a></sup> Several of these fungi are <a href="/wiki/Domestication" title="Domestication">domesticated</a> species that were <a href="/wiki/Breeding_program" title="Breeding program">bred</a> or selected according to their capacity to ferment food without producing harmful mycotoxins (see below), which are produced by very closely related <i><a href="/wiki/Aspergillus_flavus" title="Aspergillus flavus">Aspergilli</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jorgensen2007_257-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jorgensen2007-257">[257]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quorn_(food_product)" title="Quorn (food product)">Quorn</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meat_analogue" title="Meat analogue">meat substitute</a>, is made from <i><a href="/wiki/Fusarium_venenatum" title="Fusarium venenatum">Fusarium venenatum</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODonnell1998_258-0"><a href="#cite_note-ODonnell1998-258">[258]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_food">In food</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Asian_mushrooms.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="564" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Asian_mushrooms.jpg/300px-Asian_mushrooms.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Asian_mushrooms.jpg/450px-Asian_mushrooms.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Asian_mushrooms.jpg/600px-Asian_mushrooms.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Asian_mushrooms.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A selection of <a href="/wiki/Edible_mushroom" title="Edible mushroom">edible mushrooms</a> eaten in Asia</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Edible_mushroom" title="Edible mushroom">Edible mushrooms</a> include commercially raised and wild-harvested fungi. <i><a href="/wiki/Agaricus_bisporus" title="Agaricus bisporus">Agaricus bisporus</a></i>, sold as button mushrooms when small or Portobello mushrooms when larger, is the most widely cultivated species in the West, used in salads, soups, and many other dishes. Many Asian fungi are commercially grown and have increased in popularity in the West. They are often available fresh in <a href="/wiki/Grocery_store" title="Grocery store">grocery stores</a> and markets, including straw mushrooms (<i><a href="/wiki/Volvariella_volvacea" title="Volvariella volvacea">Volvariella volvacea</a></i>), oyster mushrooms (<i><a href="/wiki/Pleurotus_ostreatus" title="Pleurotus ostreatus">Pleurotus ostreatus</a></i>), shiitakes (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lentinula_edodes" title="Lentinula edodes">Lentinula edodes</a></i>), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enokitake" title="Enokitake">enokitake</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Flammulina" title="Flammulina">Flammulina</a></i> spp.).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stamets2000_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stamets2000-259">[259]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Blue_Stilton_Quarter_Front.jpg"><img alt="A corner of cheese with greenish streaks through it" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="903" decoding="async" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Blue_Stilton_Quarter_Front.jpg/220px-Blue_Stilton_Quarter_Front.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Blue_Stilton_Quarter_Front.jpg/330px-Blue_Stilton_Quarter_Front.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Blue_Stilton_Quarter_Front.jpg/440px-Blue_Stilton_Quarter_Front.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Blue_Stilton_Quarter_Front.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Stilton_cheese" title="Stilton cheese">Stilton cheese</a> veined with <i><a href="/wiki/Penicillium_roqueforti" title="Penicillium roqueforti">Penicillium roqueforti</a></i></div></div></div>
<p>Many other mushroom species are <a href="/wiki/Mushroom_hunting" title="Mushroom hunting">harvested from the wild</a> for personal consumption or commercial sale. <a href="/wiki/Lactarius_deliciosus" title="Lactarius deliciosus">Milk mushrooms</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morel" title="Morel">morels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chanterelle" title="Chanterelle">chanterelles</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Truffles" title="Truffles">truffles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Craterellus" title="Craterellus">black trumpets</a>, and <i>porcini</i> mushrooms (<i><a href="/wiki/Boletus_edulis" title="Boletus edulis">Boletus edulis</a></i>) (also known as king boletes) demand a high price on the market. They are often used in gourmet dishes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup>
</p><p>Certain types of cheeses require inoculation of milk curds with fungal species that impart a unique flavor and texture to the cheese. Examples include the <a href="/wiki/Blue_cheese" title="Blue cheese">blue</a> color in cheeses such as <a href="/wiki/Stilton_cheese" title="Stilton cheese">Stilton</a> or <a href="/wiki/Roquefort" title="Roquefort">Roquefort</a>, which are made by inoculation with <i><a href="/wiki/Penicillium_roqueforti" title="Penicillium roqueforti">Penicillium roqueforti</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kinsella1976_261-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kinsella1976-261">[261]</a></sup> Molds used in cheese production are non-toxic and are thus safe for human consumption; however, mycotoxins (e.g., aflatoxins, <a href="/wiki/Roquefortine_C" title="Roquefortine C">roquefortine C</a>, patulin, or others) may accumulate because of growth of other fungi during cheese ripening or storage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Erdogan2004_262-0"><a href="#cite_note-Erdogan2004-262">[262]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Poisonous_fungi">Poisonous fungi</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Amanita_phalloides_1.JPG"><img alt="Two light yellow-green mushrooms with stems and caps, one smaller and still in the ground, the larger one pulled out and laid beside the other to show its bulbous stem with a ring" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Amanita_phalloides_1.JPG/170px-Amanita_phalloides_1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Amanita_phalloides_1.JPG/255px-Amanita_phalloides_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Amanita_phalloides_1.JPG/340px-Amanita_phalloides_1.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Amanita_phalloides_1.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Amanita_phalloides" title="Amanita phalloides">Amanita phalloides</a></i> accounts for the majority of fatal <a href="/wiki/Mushroom_poisoning" title="Mushroom poisoning">mushroom poisonings</a> worldwide. It sometimes lacks the greenish color seen here.</div></div></div>
<p>Many mushroom species are <a href="/wiki/Mushroom_poisoning" title="Mushroom poisoning">poisonous</a> to humans and cause a range of reactions including slight digestive problems, <a href="/wiki/Allergy" title="Allergy">allergic</a> reactions, <a href="/wiki/Hallucination" title="Hallucination">hallucinations</a>, severe organ failure, and death. Genera with mushrooms containing deadly toxins include <i><a href="/wiki/Conocybe" title="Conocybe">Conocybe</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Galerina" title="Galerina">Galerina</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lepiota" title="Lepiota">Lepiota</a></i> and the most infamous, <i><a href="/wiki/Amanita" title="Amanita">Amanita</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Orr1979_263-0"><a href="#cite_note-Orr1979-263">[263]</a></sup> The latter genus includes the destroying angel <i>(<a href="/wiki/Amanita_virosa" title="Amanita virosa">A.<span class="nowrap"> </span>virosa</a>)</i> and the death cap <i>(<a href="/wiki/Amanita_phalloides" title="Amanita phalloides">A.<span class="nowrap"> </span>phalloides</a>)</i>, the most common cause of deadly mushroom poisoning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vetter1998_264-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vetter1998-264">[264]</a></sup> The false morel (<i><a href="/wiki/Gyromitra_esculenta" title="Gyromitra esculenta">Gyromitra esculenta</a></i>) is occasionally considered a delicacy when cooked, yet can be highly toxic when eaten raw.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leathem2007_265-0"><a href="#cite_note-Leathem2007-265">[265]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Tricholoma_equestre" title="Tricholoma equestre">Tricholoma equestre</a></i> was considered edible until it was implicated in serious poisonings causing <a href="/wiki/Rhabdomyolysis" title="Rhabdomyolysis">rhabdomyolysis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KarlsonStiber2003_266-0"><a href="#cite_note-KarlsonStiber2003-266">[266]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Amanita_muscaria" title="Amanita muscaria">Fly agaric</a> mushrooms (<i>Amanita muscaria</i>) also cause occasional non-fatal poisonings, mostly as a result of ingestion for its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psychedelics,_dissociatives_and_deliriants" title="Psychedelics, dissociatives and deliriants">hallucinogenic</a> properties. Historically, fly agaric was used by different peoples in Europe and Asia and its present usage for religious or <a href="/wiki/Shamanism" title="Shamanism">shamanic</a> purposes is reported from some ethnic groups such as the <a href="/wiki/Koryaks" title="Koryaks">Koryak people</a> of northeastern <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Michelot2003_267-0"><a href="#cite_note-Michelot2003-267">[267]</a></sup>
</p><p>As it is difficult to accurately identify a safe mushroom without proper training and knowledge, it is often advised to assume that a wild mushroom is poisonous and not to consume it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ammirati1987_269-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ammirati1987-269">[269]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pest_control">Pest control</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Biological_pest_control#Fungi" title="Biological pest control">Biological pest control § Fungi</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beauveria.jpg"><img alt="Two dead grasshoppers with a whitish fuzz growing on them" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1166" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Beauveria.jpg/220px-Beauveria.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Beauveria.jpg/330px-Beauveria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Beauveria.jpg/440px-Beauveria.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Beauveria.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Grasshoppers killed by <i><a href="/wiki/Beauveria_bassiana" title="Beauveria bassiana">Beauveria bassiana</a></i></div></div></div>
<p>In agriculture, fungi may be useful if they actively compete for nutrients and space with <a href="/wiki/Pathogen" title="Pathogen">pathogenic</a> microorganisms such as bacteria or other fungi via the <a href="/wiki/Competitive_exclusion_principle" title="Competitive exclusion principle">competitive exclusion principle</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LopezGomez2006_270-0"><a href="#cite_note-LopezGomez2006-270">[270]</a></sup> or if they are <a href="/wiki/Parasitism" title="Parasitism">parasites</a> of these pathogens. For example, certain species eliminate or suppress the growth of harmful plant pathogens, such as insects, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mites" title="Mites">mites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Weed" title="Weed">weeds</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nematodes" title="Nematodes">nematodes</a>, and other fungi that cause diseases of important <a href="/wiki/Crop" title="Crop">crop</a> plants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-urlUSDA_Biocontrol_271-0"><a href="#cite_note-urlUSDA_Biocontrol-271">[271]</a></sup> This has generated strong interest in practical applications that use these fungi in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biological_control" title="Biological control">biological control</a> of these agricultural pests. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Entomopathogenic_fungi" title="Entomopathogenic fungi">Entomopathogenic fungi</a> can be used as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biopesticides" title="Biopesticides">biopesticides</a>, as they actively kill insects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chandler_2017_272-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chandler_2017-272">[272]</a></sup> Examples that have been used as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biological_insecticide" title="Biological insecticide">biological insecticides</a> are <i><a href="/wiki/Beauveria_bassiana" title="Beauveria bassiana">Beauveria bassiana</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Metarhizium" title="Metarhizium">Metarhizium</a></i> spp., <i><a href="/wiki/Hirsutella" title="Hirsutella">Hirsutella</a></i> spp., <i><a href="/wiki/Paecilomyces" title="Paecilomyces">Paecilomyces</a></i> (<i>Isaria</i>) spp., and <i><a href="/wiki/Lecanicillium_lecanii" title="Lecanicillium lecanii">Lecanicillium lecanii</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deshpande1999_273-0"><a href="#cite_note-Deshpande1999-273">[273]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thomas2007_274-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas2007-274">[274]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endophytic" title="Endophytic">Endophytic</a> fungi of grasses of the genus <i><a href="/wiki/Epichlo%C3%AB" title="Epichloë">Epichloë</a></i>, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Epichlo%C3%AB_coenophiala" title="Epichloë coenophiala">E. coenophiala</a></i>, produce alkaloids that are toxic to a range of invertebrate and vertebrate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herbivores" title="Herbivores">herbivores</a>. These alkaloids protect grass plants from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herbivory" title="Herbivory">herbivory</a>, but several endophyte alkaloids can poison grazing animals, such as cattle and sheep.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guerre_2015_275-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guerre_2015-275">[275]</a></sup> Infecting cultivars of <a href="/wiki/Pasture" title="Pasture">pasture</a> or <a href="/wiki/Forage" title="Forage">forage</a> grasses with <i>Epichloë</i> endophytes is one approach being used in <a href="/wiki/Plant_breeding" title="Plant breeding">grass breeding</a> programs; the fungal strains are selected for producing only alkaloids that increase resistance to herbivores such as insects, while being non-toxic to livestock.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bouton2002_276-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bouton2002-276">[276]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Parish2003_277-0"><a href="#cite_note-Parish2003-277">[277]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bioremediation">Bioremediation</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mycoremediation" title="Mycoremediation">Mycoremediation</a></div>
<p>Certain fungi, in particular <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_rot" title="White rot">white-rot</a> fungi, can degrade <a href="/wiki/Insecticide" title="Insecticide">insecticides</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herbicide" title="Herbicide">herbicides</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pentachlorophenol" title="Pentachlorophenol">pentachlorophenol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Creosote" title="Creosote">creosote</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coal_tar" title="Coal tar">coal tars</a>, and heavy fuels and turn them into <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a>, water, and basic elements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zhuo_&amp;_Fan_2021_278-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zhuo_&amp;_Fan_2021-278">[278]</a></sup> Fungi have been shown to <a href="/wiki/Biomineralization" title="Biomineralization">biomineralize</a> <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a> <a href="/wiki/Oxide" title="Oxide">oxides</a>, suggesting they may have application in the <a href="/wiki/Bioremediation" title="Bioremediation">bioremediation</a> of radioactively polluted sites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC2008_279-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC2008-279">[279]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fomina2007_280-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fomina2007-280">[280]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fomina2008_281-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fomina2008-281">[281]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Model_organisms">Model organisms</span></h3>
<p>Several pivotal discoveries in biology were made by researchers using fungi as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Model_organisms" title="Model organisms">model organisms</a>, that is, fungi that grow and sexually reproduce rapidly in the laboratory. For example, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/One_gene-one_enzyme_hypothesis" title="One gene-one enzyme hypothesis">one gene-one enzyme hypothesis</a> was formulated by scientists using the bread mold <i><a href="/wiki/Neurospora_crassa" title="Neurospora crassa">Neurospora crassa</a></i> to test their biochemical theories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beadle1941_282-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beadle1941-282">[282]</a></sup> Other important model fungi are <i><a href="/wiki/Aspergillus_nidulans" title="Aspergillus nidulans">Aspergillus nidulans</a></i> and the yeasts <i><a href="/wiki/Saccharomyces_cerevisiae" title="Saccharomyces cerevisiae">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Schizosaccharomyces_pombe" title="Schizosaccharomyces pombe">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</a></i>, each of which with a long history of use to investigate issues in eukaryotic <a href="/wiki/Cell_biology" title="Cell biology">cell biology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">genetics</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Cell_cycle" title="Cell cycle">cell cycle</a> regulation, <a href="/wiki/Chromatin" title="Chromatin">chromatin</a> structure, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gene_regulation" title="Gene regulation">gene regulation</a>. Other fungal models have emerged that address specific biological questions relevant to <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plant_pathology" title="Plant pathology">plant pathology</a>, and industrial uses; examples include <i><a href="/wiki/Candida_albicans" title="Candida albicans">Candida albicans</a></i>, a dimorphic, opportunistic human pathogen,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Datta1989_283-0"><a href="#cite_note-Datta1989-283">[283]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Magnaporthe_grisea" title="Magnaporthe grisea">Magnaporthe grisea</a></i>, a plant pathogen,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dean2005_284-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dean2005-284">[284]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Pichia_pastoris" title="Pichia pastoris">Pichia pastoris</a></i>, a yeast widely used for eukaryotic <a href="/wiki/Protein_production" title="Protein production">protein production</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karbalaei_et_al._2020_285-0"><a href="#cite_note-Karbalaei_et_al._2020-285">[285]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Others">Others</span></h3>
<p>Fungi are used extensively to produce industrial chemicals like <a href="/wiki/Citric_acid" title="Citric acid">citric</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gluconic_acid" title="Gluconic acid">gluconic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lactic_acid" title="Lactic acid">lactic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Malic_acid" title="Malic acid">malic</a> acids,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schlegel1993_286-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schlegel1993-286">[286]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Industrial_enzymes" title="Industrial enzymes">industrial enzymes</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Lipase" title="Lipase">lipases</a> used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biological_detergent" title="Biological detergent">biological detergents</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Joseph2008_287-0"><a href="#cite_note-Joseph2008-287">[287]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cellulase" title="Cellulase">cellulases</a> used in making <a href="/wiki/Cellulosic_ethanol" title="Cellulosic ethanol">cellulosic ethanol</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kumar2008_288-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kumar2008-288">[288]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stonewashed_jeans" title="Stonewashed jeans">stonewashed jeans</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nysaes_289-0"><a href="#cite_note-nysaes-289">[289]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Amylase" title="Amylase">amylases</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OlempskaBeer2006_290-0"><a href="#cite_note-OlempskaBeer2006-290">[290]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Invertase" title="Invertase">invertases</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protease" title="Protease">proteases</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xylanase" title="Xylanase">xylanases</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Polizeli2005_291-0"><a href="#cite_note-Polizeli2005-291">[291]</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://www.iucn.org/sites/dev/files/statement-3f.pdf" rel="nofollow">"IUCN SSC acceptance of Fauna Flora Funga"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. Fungal Conservation Committee, IUCN SSC. 2021. <q>The IUCN Species Survival Commission calls for the due recognition of fungi as major components of biodiversity in legislation and policy. It fully endorses the Fauna Flora Funga Initiative and asks that the phrases <b>animals and plants</b> and <b>fauna and flora</b> be replaced with <b>animals, fungi, and plants</b> and <b>fauna, flora, and funga</b>.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=IUCN+SSC+acceptance+of+Fauna+Flora+Funga&amp;rft.pub=Fungal+Conservation+Committee%2C+IUCN+SSC&amp;rft.date=2021&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.iucn.org%2Fsites%2Fdev%2Ffiles%2Fstatement-3f.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFungus"></span></span>
</li>
